<p>The <b>California Institute of Technology</b> (abbreviated <b>Caltech</b><sup id="cite_ref-caltech_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caltech-6">[6]</a></sup>) is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a> <a href="/wiki/Doctorate-granting_university" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctorate-granting university">doctorate-granting university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a>, United States. Although founded as a preparatory and vocational school by <a href="/wiki/Amos_G._Throop" title="Amos G. Throop">Amos G. Throop</a> in 1891, the college attracted influential scientists such as <a href="/wiki/George_Ellery_Hale" title="George Ellery Hale">George Ellery Hale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Amos_Noyes" title="Arthur Amos Noyes">Arthur Amos Noyes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Andrews_Millikan" title="Robert Andrews Millikan">Robert Andrews Millikan</a> in the early 20th century. The vocational and preparatory schools were disbanded and spun off in 1910, and the college assumed its present name in 1921. In 1934, Caltech was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, and the antecedents of <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a>, which Caltech continues to manage and operate, were established between 1936 and 1943 under <a href="/wiki/Theodore_von_K%C3%A1rm%C3%A1n" title="Theodore von Kármán">Theodore von Kármán</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aau_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aau-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The university is one among a small group of <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Technology_(United_States)" title="Institute of Technology (United States)">Institutes of Technology in the United States</a> which is primarily devoted to the instruction of technical arts and applied sciences.</p>
<p>Caltech has six academic divisions with strong emphasis on science and engineering, managing $332 million in 2011 in sponsored research.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-9">[9]</a></sup> Its 124-acre (50&#160;ha) primary campus is located approximately 11&#160;mi (18&#160;km) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Los_Angeles" title="Downtown Los Angeles">downtown Los Angeles</a>. First-year students are required to live on campus, and 95% of undergraduates remain in the on-campus <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_Caltech" class="mw-redirect" title="House System at Caltech">House System at Caltech</a>. Although Caltech has a strong tradition of practical jokes and pranks,<sup id="cite_ref-geek_pranks_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geek_pranks-10">[10]</a></sup> student life is governed by an honor code which allows faculty to assign <a href="/wiki/Final_examination#Take-home_finals" title="Final examination">take-home examinations</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Caltech_Beavers" class="mw-redirect" title="Caltech Beavers">Caltech Beavers</a> compete in 13 intercollegiate sports in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Intercollegiate_Athletic_Conference" title="Southern California Intercollegiate Athletic Conference">Southern California Intercollegiate Athletic Conference</a>.</p>
<p>Caltech is frequently cited as one of the world's best universities.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Caltech alumni and faculty include 34 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prizes" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prizes">Nobel Prizes</a> (<a href="/wiki/Linus_Pauling" title="Linus Pauling">Linus Pauling</a> being the only individual in history to win two unshared prizes), <a href="/wiki/List_of_Fields_Medal_winners_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Fields Medal winners by university affiliation">1 Fields Medalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Turing_Award_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Turing Award laureates by university affiliation">6 Turing Award winners</a>, 4 <a href="/wiki/Chief_Scientist_of_the_U.S._Air_Force" title="Chief Scientist of the U.S. Air Force">Chief Scientists of the U.S. Air Force</a> and 71&#160;have won the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a> or <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="National Medal of Technology">Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-at_a_glance_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at_a_glance-4">[4]</a></sup> There are 112 faculty members who have been elected to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academies" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Academies">United States National Academies</a>. In addition, numerous faculty members are associated with the <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes_Medical_Institute" title="Howard Hughes Medical Institute">Howard Hughes Medical Institute</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-at_a_glance_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at_a_glance-4">[4]</a></sup> According to a 2015 Pomona College study, Caltech ranked number one in the U.S. for the percentage of its graduates who go on to earn a PhD.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Throop_College">Throop College</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Throop College">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Throop_Polytechnic_Institute,_Pasadena,_Calif.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Throop_Polytechnic_Institute%2C_Pasadena%2C_Calif.jpg/280px-Throop_Polytechnic_Institute%2C_Pasadena%2C_Calif.jpg" width="280" height="62" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Throop_Polytechnic_Institute%2C_Pasadena%2C_Calif.jpg/420px-Throop_Polytechnic_Institute%2C_Pasadena%2C_Calif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Throop_Polytechnic_Institute%2C_Pasadena%2C_Calif.jpg/560px-Throop_Polytechnic_Institute%2C_Pasadena%2C_Calif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1744" data-file-height="388" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Throop_Polytechnic_Institute,_Pasadena,_Calif.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Throop Polytechnic Institute, Pasadena, California, 1908, on its original campus at downtown Pasadena</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Caltech started as a <a href="/wiki/Vocational_school" title="Vocational school">vocational school</a> founded in Pasadena in 1891 by local businessman and politician <a href="/wiki/Amos_G._Throop" title="Amos G. Throop">Amos G. Throop</a>. The school was known successively as <b>Throop University</b>, <b>Throop Polytechnic Institute</b> (and Manual Training School),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and <b>Throop College of Technology</b>, before acquiring its current name in 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-incorporation_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incorporation-15">[15]</a></sup> The vocational school was disbanded and the preparatory program was split off to form an independent <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_School" title="Polytechnic School">Polytechnic School</a> in 1907.</p>
<p>At a time when scientific research in the United States was still in its infancy, <a href="/wiki/George_Ellery_Hale" title="George Ellery Hale">George Ellery Hale</a>, a solar astronomer from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, founded the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Wilson_Observatory" title="Mount Wilson Observatory">Mount Wilson Observatory</a> in 1904. He joined Throop's board of trustees in 1907, and soon began developing it and the whole of Pasadena into a major scientific and cultural destination. He engineered the appointment of <a href="/wiki/James_Augustin_Brown_Scherer" title="James Augustin Brown Scherer">James A. B. Scherer</a>, a literary scholar untutored in science but a capable administrator and fund raiser, to Throop's presidency in 1908. Scherer persuaded retired businessman and trustee Charles W. Gates to donate $25,000 in seed money to build Gates Laboratory, the first science building on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-gates_lab_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gates_lab-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wars">World Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: World Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1910, Throop moved to its current site. Arther Fleming donated the land for the permanent campus site. <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> delivered an address at Throop Institute on March 21, 1911, and he declared:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>I want to see institutions like Throop turn out perhaps ninety-nine of every hundred students as men who are to do given pieces of industrial work better than any one else can do them; I want to see those men do the kind of work that is now being done on the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a> and on the great irrigation projects in the interior of this country—and the one-hundredth man I want to see with the kind of cultural scientific training that will make him and his fellows the matrix out of which you can occasionally develop a man like your great astronomer, George Ellery Hale.<sup id="cite_ref-Caltech_Catalog_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caltech_Catalog-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Throop_Hall_at_Cal_Tech,_in_Pasadena_(00035486).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Throop_Hall_at_Cal_Tech%2C_in_Pasadena_%2800035486%29.jpg/220px-Throop_Hall_at_Cal_Tech%2C_in_Pasadena_%2800035486%29.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Throop_Hall_at_Cal_Tech%2C_in_Pasadena_%2800035486%29.jpg/330px-Throop_Hall_at_Cal_Tech%2C_in_Pasadena_%2800035486%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Throop_Hall_at_Cal_Tech%2C_in_Pasadena_%2800035486%29.jpg/440px-Throop_Hall_at_Cal_Tech%2C_in_Pasadena_%2800035486%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="490" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Throop_Hall_at_Cal_Tech,_in_Pasadena_(00035486).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Throop Hall, 1912</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the same year, a bill was introduced in the <a href="/wiki/California_Legislature" class="mw-redirect" title="California Legislature">California Legislature</a> calling for the establishment of a publicly funded "California Institute of Technology", with an initial budget of a million dollars, ten times the budget of Throop at the time. The board of trustees offered to turn Throop over to the state, but the presidents of <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> successfully lobbied to defeat the bill, which allowed Throop to develop as the only scientific research-oriented education institute in southern California, public or private, until the onset of the World War II necessitated the broader development of research-based science education.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Dream_Endures_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Dream_Endures-18">[18]</a></sup> The promise of Throop attracted <a href="/wiki/Physical_chemistry" title="Physical chemistry">physical chemist</a> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Amos_Noyes" title="Arthur Amos Noyes">Arthur Amos Noyes</a> from <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a> to develop the institution and assist in establishing it as a center for science and technology.</p>
<p>With the onset of World War I, Hale organized the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Research Council">National Research Council</a> to coordinate and support scientific work on military problems. While he supported the idea of federal appropriations for science, he took exception to a federal bill that would have funded engineering research at land-grant colleges, and instead sought to raise a $1 million national research fund entirely from private sources. To that end, as Hale wrote in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Throop College of Technology, in Pasadena California has recently afforded a striking illustration of one way in which the Research Council can secure co-operation and advance scientific investigation. This institution, with its able investigators and excellent research laboratories, could be of great service in any broad scheme of cooperation. President Scherer, hearing of the formation of the council, immediately offered to take part in its work, and with this object, he secured within three days an additional research endowment of one hundred thousand dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-NRC_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Through the National Research Council, Hale simultaneously lobbied for science to play a larger role in national affairs, and for Throop to play a national role in science. The new funds were designated for physics research, and ultimately led to the establishment of the Norman Bridge Laboratory, which attracted experimental <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physicist</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Andrews_Millikan" title="Robert Andrews Millikan">Robert Andrews Millikan</a> from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> in 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_lab_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge_lab-20">[20]</a></sup> During the course of the war, Hale, Noyes and Millikan worked together in Washington on the NRC. Subsequently, they continued their partnership in developing Caltech.<sup id="cite_ref-NRC_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:648px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caltech_Entrance.jpg" class="image" title="Caltech entrance at 1200 E California Blvd. On the left is East Norman Bridge Laboratory of Physics and on the right is the Alfred Sloan Laboratory of Mathematics and Physics."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Caltech_Entrance.jpg/640px-Caltech_Entrance.jpg" width="640" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Caltech_Entrance.jpg/960px-Caltech_Entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Caltech_Entrance.jpg/1280px-Caltech_Entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="596" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caltech_Entrance.jpg" title="File:Caltech Entrance.jpg"></a></div>
Caltech entrance at 1200 E California Blvd. On the left is East Norman Bridge Laboratory of Physics and on the right is the Alfred Sloan Laboratory of Mathematics and Physics.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under the leadership of Hale, Noyes and Millikan (aided by the booming economy of <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>), Caltech grew to national prominence in the 1920s and concentrated on the development of Roosevelt's "Hundredth Man". On November 29, 1921, the trustees declared it to be the express policy of the Institute to pursue scientific research of the greatest importance and at the same time "to continue to conduct thorough courses in engineering and pure science, basing the work of these courses on exceptionally strong instruction in the fundamental sciences of mathematics, physics, and chemistry; broadening and enriching the curriculum by a liberal amount of instruction in such subjects as English, history, and economics; and vitalizing all the work of the Institute by the infusion in generous measure of the spirit of research."<sup id="cite_ref-Caltech_Catalog_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caltech_Catalog-17">[17]</a></sup> In 1923, Millikan was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a>. In 1925, the school established a department of geology and hired <a href="/wiki/William_Bennett_Munro" class="mw-redirect" title="William Bennett Munro">William Bennett Munro</a>, then chairman of the division of History, Government, and Economics at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, to create a division of <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social sciences</a> at Caltech. In 1928, a division of <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a> was established under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hunt_Morgan" title="Thomas Hunt Morgan">Thomas Hunt Morgan</a>, the most distinguished biologist in the United States at the time, and discoverer of the role of genes and the <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosome</a> in heredity. In 1930, <a href="/wiki/Kerckhoff_Marine_Laboratory" title="Kerckhoff Marine Laboratory">Kerckhoff Marine Laboratory</a> was established in Corona del Mar under the care of Professor George MacGinitie. In 1926, a graduate school of <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">aeronautics</a> was created, which eventually attracted <a href="/wiki/Theodore_von_K%C3%A1rm%C3%A1n" title="Theodore von Kármán">Theodore von Kármán</a>. Kármán later helped create the Jet Propulsion Laboratory, and played an integral part in establishing Caltech as one of the world's centers for <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rocket science</a>. In 1928, construction of the <a href="/wiki/Palomar_Observatory" title="Palomar Observatory">Palomar Observatory</a> began.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tolman_%26_Einstein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Tolman_%26_Einstein.jpg/220px-Tolman_%26_Einstein.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Tolman_%26_Einstein.jpg/330px-Tolman_%26_Einstein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Tolman_%26_Einstein.jpg/440px-Tolman_%26_Einstein.jpg 2x" data-file-width="690" data-file-height="470" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tolman_%26_Einstein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Richard_C._Tolman" title="Richard C. Tolman">Richard C. Tolman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> at Caltech, 1932</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Millikan served as "Chairman of the Executive Council" (effectively Caltech's president) from 1921 to 1945, and his influence was such that the Institute was occasionally referred to as "Millikan's School." Millikan initiated a visiting-scholars program soon after joining Caltech. Scientists who accepted his invitation include luminaries such as <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dirac" title="Paul Dirac">Paul Dirac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Schr%C3%B6dinger" title="Erwin Schrödinger">Erwin Schrödinger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Werner_Heisenberg" title="Werner Heisenberg">Werner Heisenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Lorentz" title="Hendrik Lorentz">Hendrik Lorentz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niels_Bohr" title="Niels Bohr">Niels Bohr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> arrived on the Caltech campus for the first time in 1931 to polish up his <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_General_Relativity" class="mw-redirect" title="Theory of General Relativity">Theory of General Relativity</a>, and he returned to Caltech subsequently as a visiting professor in 1932 and 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>During World War II, Caltech was one of 131 colleges and universities nationally that took part in the <a href="/wiki/V-12_Navy_College_Training_Program" title="V-12 Navy College Training Program">V-12 Navy College Training Program</a> which offered students a path to a Navy commission.<sup id="cite_ref-caltech-v-12_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caltech-v-12-23">[23]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> also maintained a naval training school for <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Aeronautical engineering">aeronautical engineering</a>, resident inspectors of ordnance and naval material, and a liaison officer to the <a href="/wiki/National_Defense_Research_Committee" title="National Defense Research Committee">National Defense Research Committee</a> on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_growth">Post-war growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post-war growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beckman_Institute_Reflection.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Beckman_Institute_Reflection.jpg/220px-Beckman_Institute_Reflection.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Beckman_Institute_Reflection.jpg/330px-Beckman_Institute_Reflection.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Beckman_Institute_Reflection.jpg/440px-Beckman_Institute_Reflection.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beckman_Institute_Reflection.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Beckman_Institute_at_Caltech" title="Beckman Institute at Caltech">Beckman Institute at Caltech</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1950s–1970s, Caltech was the home of <a href="/wiki/Murray_Gell-Mann" title="Murray Gell-Mann">Murray Gell-Mann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Feynman" title="Richard Feynman">Richard Feynman</a>, whose work was central to the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Model" title="Standard Model">Standard Model</a> of particle physics. Feynman was also widely known outside the physics community as an exceptional teacher and colorful, unconventional character.</p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/Lee_A._DuBridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Lee A. DuBridge">Lee A. DuBridge</a>'s tenure as Caltech's president (1946–1969), Caltech's faculty doubled and the campus tripled in size. DuBridge, unlike his predecessors, welcomed <a href="/wiki/Federal_funding" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal funding">federal funding</a> of science. New research fields flourished, including <a href="/wiki/Chemical_biology" title="Chemical biology">chemical biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Planetary_science" title="Planetary science">planetary science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_astrophysics" title="Nuclear astrophysics">nuclear astrophysics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geochemistry" title="Geochemistry">geochemistry</a>. A 200-inch telescope was dedicated on nearby Palomar Mountain in 1948 and remained the world's most powerful optical telescope for over forty years.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Caltech opened its doors to female undergraduates during the presidency of <a href="/wiki/Harold_Brown_(Secretary_of_Defense)" title="Harold Brown (Secretary of Defense)">Harold Brown</a> in 1970, and they made up 14% of the entering class.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The fraction of female undergraduates has been increasing since then.<sup id="cite_ref-at_a_glance_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at_a_glance-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Caltech undergraduates have historically been so apathetic to politics<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="Who says this? (July 2014)">weasel&#160;words</span></a></i>]</sup> that there has been only one organized student protest in January 1968 outside the Burbank studios of <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>, in response to rumors that NBC was to cancel <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">Star Trek</a>. In 1973, the students from <a href="/wiki/Dabney_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Dabney House">Dabney House</a> protested a presidential visit with a sign on the library bearing the simple phrase "<a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Impeach Nixon</a>". The following week, Ross McCollum, president of the <a href="/wiki/National_Oil_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="National Oil Company">National Oil Company</a>, wrote an open letter to Dabney House stating that in light of their actions he had decided not to donate one million dollars to Caltech. The Dabney family, being Republicans, disowned Dabney House after hearing of the prank.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Einstein_Papers_Project" title="Einstein Papers Project">Einstein Papers Project</a> has been located at Caltech.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The project was established in 1986 to assemble, preserve, translate, and publish papers selected from the literary estate of Albert Einstein and from other collections.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Annenberg_center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Annenberg_center.jpg/220px-Annenberg_center.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Annenberg_center.jpg/330px-Annenberg_center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Annenberg_center.jpg/440px-Annenberg_center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Annenberg_center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The new Annenberg Center for Information Science and Technology</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In fall 2008, the freshman class was 42% female, a record for Caltech's undergraduate enrollment.<sup id="cite_ref-at_a_glance_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at_a_glance-4">[4]</a></sup> In the same year, the Institute concluded a six-year-long fund-raising campaign. The campaign raised more than $1.4 billion from about 16,000 donors. Nearly half of the funds went into the support of Caltech programs and projects.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Caltech, in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Berkeley_National_Laboratory" title="Lawrence Berkeley National Laboratory">Lawrence Berkeley National Laboratory</a> and headed by Professor <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Lewis" title="Nathan Lewis">Nathan Lewis</a>, established a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">DOE</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy#Energy_Innovation_Hubs" title="United States Department of Energy">Energy Innovation Hub</a> aimed at developing revolutionary methods to generate fuels directly from sunlight. This hub, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Center_for_Artificial_Photosynthesis" title="Joint Center for Artificial Photosynthesis">Joint Center for Artificial Photosynthesis</a>, will receive up to $122 million in federal funding over five years.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2012, Caltech began to offer classes through <a href="/wiki/Massive_open_online_course" title="Massive open online course">massive open online courses</a> (MOOCs) under <a href="/wiki/Coursera" title="Coursera">Coursera</a>, and from 2013, <a href="/wiki/EdX" title="EdX">edX</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jean-Lou Chameau, the eighth president, announced on February 19, 2013, that he would be stepping down to accept the presidency at <a href="/wiki/King_Abdullah_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="King Abdullah University of Science and Technology">King Abdullah University of Science and Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Felix_Rosenbaum" title="Thomas Felix Rosenbaum">Thomas F. Rosenbaum</a> was announced to be the ninth president of Caltech on October 24, 2013, and his term began on July 1, 2014.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_California_Institute_of_Technology_buildings_and_facilities" title="List of California Institute of Technology buildings and facilities">List of California Institute of Technology buildings and facilities</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_A._Millikan_Memorial_Library_at_Caltech.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Robert_A._Millikan_Memorial_Library_at_Caltech.jpg/220px-Robert_A._Millikan_Memorial_Library_at_Caltech.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Robert_A._Millikan_Memorial_Library_at_Caltech.jpg/330px-Robert_A._Millikan_Memorial_Library_at_Caltech.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Robert_A._Millikan_Memorial_Library_at_Caltech.jpg/440px-Robert_A._Millikan_Memorial_Library_at_Caltech.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_A._Millikan_Memorial_Library_at_Caltech.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Millikan Library, the tallest building on campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Caltech's 124-acre (50&#160;ha) primary campus is located in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a>, approximately 11 miles (18&#160;km) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Los_Angeles" title="Downtown Los Angeles">downtown Los Angeles</a>. It is within walking distance of <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Pasadena" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Town Pasadena">Old Town Pasadena</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Playhouse_District,_Pasadena,_California" title="Playhouse District, Pasadena, California">Pasadena Playhouse District</a> and therefore the two locations are frequent getaways for Caltech students.</p>
<p>In 1917 Hale hired architect <a href="/wiki/Bertram_Goodhue" title="Bertram Goodhue">Bertram Goodhue</a> to produce a master plan for the 22 acres (8.9&#160;ha) campus. Goodhue conceived the overall layout of the campus and designed the physics building, Dabney Hall, and several other structures, in which he sought to be consistent with the local climate, the character of the school, and Hale's educational philosophy. Goodhue's designs for Caltech were also influenced by the traditional <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_the_California_Missions" class="mw-redirect" title="Architecture of the California Missions">Spanish mission architecture</a> of Southern California.</p>
<p>In 1971 a <a href="/wiki/1971_San_Fernando_earthquake" title="1971 San Fernando earthquake">magnitude-6.6 earthquake</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_California" title="San Fernando, California">San Fernando</a> caused some damage to the Caltech campus. Engineers who evaluated the damage found that two historic buildings dating from the early days of the Institute—Throop Hall and the Goodhue-designed Culbertson Auditorium—had cracked. These were some of the first <a href="/wiki/Reinforced_concrete" title="Reinforced concrete">reinforced concrete</a> buildings, and their plans did not contain enough details (such as how much <a href="/wiki/Rebar" title="Rebar">reinforcing bar</a> had been embedded in the concrete) to be sure they were safe, so the engineers recommended demolition. However, demolishing these historic structures required considerably more effort than would have been necessary had they been in real danger of collapse. A large <a href="/wiki/Wrecking_ball" title="Wrecking ball">wrecking ball</a> was used to demolish Throop Hall, and smashing the concrete revealed massive amounts of rebar, far in excess of safety requirements. The rebar had to be cut up before the pieces could be hauled away, and the process took much longer than expected.</p>
<p>New additions to the campus include the Cahill Center for Astronomy and Astrophysics and the <a href="/wiki/Walter_Annenberg" title="Walter Annenberg">Walter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonore_Annenberg" title="Leonore Annenberg">Leonore Annenberg</a> Center for Information Science and Technology, which opened in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and the Warren and Katherine Schlinger Laboratory for Chemistry and Chemical Engineering followed in March 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The Institute also concluded an upgrading of the <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology#South_Houses" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">south houses</a> in 2006. In late 2010, Caltech completed a 1.3 MW <a href="/wiki/Solar_array" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar array">solar array</a> projected to produce approximately 1.6 GWh in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_California_Institute_of_Technology_trustees" title="List of California Institute of Technology trustees">List of California Institute of Technology trustees</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Norman_Bridge_Lab_Interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Norman_Bridge_Lab_Interior.jpg/220px-Norman_Bridge_Lab_Interior.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Norman_Bridge_Lab_Interior.jpg/330px-Norman_Bridge_Lab_Interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Norman_Bridge_Lab_Interior.jpg/440px-Norman_Bridge_Lab_Interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Norman_Bridge_Lab_Interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bridge Laboratory of Physics</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The mission statement of Caltech reads:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The mission of the California Institute of Technology is to expand human knowledge and benefit society through research integrated with education. We investigate the most challenging, fundamental problems in science and technology in a singularly collegial, interdisciplinary atmosphere, while educating outstanding students to become creative members of society.<sup id="cite_ref-at_a_glance_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at_a_glance-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Caltech is incorporated as a non-profit corporation and is governed by a privately appointed 46-member <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board of trustees</a> who serve five-year terms of office and retire at the age of 72.<sup id="cite_ref-incorporation_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incorporation-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bylaws_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bylaws-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_California_Institute_of_Technology_trustees" title="List of California Institute of Technology trustees">The current board</a> is chaired by <a href="/wiki/David_L._Lee" title="David L. Lee">David L. Lee</a>, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Global_Crossing_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="Global Crossing Ltd.">Global Crossing Ltd.</a> The Trustees elect a President to serve as the chief executive officer of the Institute and administer the affairs on the Institute on behalf of the board, a Provost who serves as the chief academic officer of the Institute below the President, and ten other vice presidential and other senior positions.<sup id="cite_ref-bylaws_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bylaws-37">[37]</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Institute_of_Technology" title="Georgia Institute of Technology">Georgia Tech</a> provost <a href="/wiki/Jean-Lou_Chameau" title="Jean-Lou Chameau">Jean-Lou Chameau</a> became the eighth president of Caltech on September 1, 2006, replacing <a href="/wiki/David_Baltimore" title="David Baltimore">David Baltimore</a> who had served since 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Dr. Chameau's compensation for 2008–2009 totaled $799,472.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Chameau served until June 30, 2013. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Felix_Rosenbaum" title="Thomas Felix Rosenbaum">Thomas F. Rosenbaum</a> was announced to be the ninth president of Caltech on October 24, 2013, and his term began on July 1, 2014. Caltech's endowment is governed by a permanent Trustee committee and administered by an Investment Office.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kerckhoff_Laboratory_of_the_Biological_Sciences.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kerckhoff_Laboratory_of_the_Biological_Sciences.jpg/220px-Kerckhoff_Laboratory_of_the_Biological_Sciences.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kerckhoff_Laboratory_of_the_Biological_Sciences.jpg/330px-Kerckhoff_Laboratory_of_the_Biological_Sciences.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kerckhoff_Laboratory_of_the_Biological_Sciences.jpg/440px-Kerckhoff_Laboratory_of_the_Biological_Sciences.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kerckhoff_Laboratory_of_the_Biological_Sciences.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Kerckhoff Laboratory of the Biological Sciences</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Institute is organized into six primary academic divisions: Biology and Biological Engineering, Chemistry and Chemical Engineering, Engineering and Applied Science, Geological and Planetary Sciences, Humanities and Social Sciences, and Physics, Mathematics, and Astronomy. The voting faculty of Caltech include all professors, instructors, research associates and fellows, and the University Librarian. Faculty are responsible for establishing admission requirements, academic standards, and curricula. The Faculty Board is the faculty's representative body and consists of 18 elected faculty representatives as well as other senior administration officials. Full-time professors are expected to teach classes, conduct research, advise students, and perform administrative work such as serving on committees.<sup id="cite_ref-faculty_handbook_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faculty_handbook-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> (JPL) is a <a href="/wiki/Federally_funded_research_and_development_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Federally funded research and development center">federally funded research and development center</a> (FFRDC) owned by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> and operated as a division of Caltech through a contract between NASA and Caltech. In 2008, JPL spent over $1.6&#160;billion on research and development and employed over 5,000 project-related and support employees.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The JPL Director also serves as a Caltech Vice President and is responsible to the President of the Institute for the management of the laboratory.<sup id="cite_ref-officers_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officers-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td>5</td>
