<p>Caltech is a small four-year, highly residential research university with a slight majority in graduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-carnegie_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carnegie-51">[51]</a></sup> The Institute has been accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Western_Association_of_Schools_and_Colleges" title="Western Association of Schools and Colleges">Western Association of Schools and Colleges</a> since 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Caltech is on the <a href="/wiki/Academic_term" title="Academic term">quarter system</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-cds_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cds-54">[54]</a></sup> the fall term starts in late September and ends before Christmas, the second term starts after New Years Day and ends in mid-March, and the third term starts in late March or early April and ends in early June.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Caltech is ranked 1st internationally since 2011 by the <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Caltech was ranked as the best university in the world in two categories: Engineering &amp; Technology and Physical Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> It was also found to have the highest faculty citation rate in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> (ARWU), a ranking with an emphasis on bibliometric data and scientific research, ranked Caltech 8th in the world and 6th in the U.S. for 2016.</p>
<p>In 2012, the Center for World University Rankings ranked Caltech fifth in the world and fourth nationally in its CWUR World University Rankings.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Money_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Money Magazine">Money Magazine</a></i> ranked Caltech 10th in the country out of the nearly 1500 schools it evaluated for its 2014 Best Colleges ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> ranked Caltech 12th in the country out of the nearly 2000 schools it evaluated for its 2014 Best Colleges ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked Caltech as tied for the 10th best university in the United States in their 2016 national rankings, with the graduate programs in chemistry and earth sciences ranked first in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Research Council">United States National Research Council</a> released its latest <i>Assessment of Research Doctorate Programs</i> in 2010, and 23 of the 24 graduate programs of Caltech were ranked within the top four programs in the nation in their size quartile as determined by both the R95 and S95 rankings. Of particular note, programs that were placed within the top 10% of all size programs in that field based on an average of the R95 and S95 rank order include Aeronautics, Astrophysics, Biochemistry and Molecular Biophysics, Bioengineering, Biology, Chemical Engineering, Chemistry, Electrical Engineering, Environmental Science and Engineering, Geology, Geophysics, Materials Science, Mechanical Engineering, Physics, Planetary Science, and Social Science (Economics).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013 a paper published in the <a href="/wiki/Quarterly_Journal_of_Economics" title="Quarterly Journal of Economics">Quarterly Journal of Economics</a> ranked Caltech 2nd in the U.S. (after <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>) for revealed preference.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The sample of the study was 3240 high achieving students (students ranked in the top 10% of public high school class or top 20% of private high school class). Rankings were based on number of students who accepted offered admission.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For the Class of 2019 (enrolled fall 2015), Caltech received 6,506 applications and accepted 573 (8.8%); 241 enrolled, a yield rate (the percentage of accepted students who enroll) of 42.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-CommonDataSet_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CommonDataSet-65">[65]</a></sup> The middle 50% range of <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores for enrolled freshmen were 730-800 for critical reading, 770-800 for math, and 730-790 for writing. The middle 50% range <a href="/wiki/ACT_(test)" title="ACT (test)">ACT</a> Composite score was 34-35.<sup id="cite_ref-CommonDataSet_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CommonDataSet-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuition_and_financial_aid">Tuition and financial aid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tuition and financial aid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Undergraduate tuition for the 2013–2014 school year was $39,990 and total annual costs were estimated to be $58,755.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In 2012–2013, Caltech awarded $17.1 million in need-based aid, $438k in non-need-based aid, and $2.51 million in self-help support to enrolled undergraduate student. The average financial aid package of all students eligible for aid was $38,756 and students graduated with an average debt of $15,090.<sup id="cite_ref-cds_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cds-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_program">Undergraduate program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Undergraduate program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The full-time, four-year undergraduate program emphasizes instruction in the arts and sciences and has high graduate coexistence.<sup id="cite_ref-carnegie_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carnegie-51">[51]</a></sup> Caltech offers 24 majors (called "options") and six minors across all six academic divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Caltech also offers interdisciplinary programs in Applied Physics, Biochemistry, Bioengineering, Computation and Neural Systems, Control and Dynamical Systems, Environmental Science and Engineering, Geobiology and Astrobiology, Geochemistry, and Planetary Astronomy. The most popular options are Chemical Engineering, Computer Science, Electrical Engineering, Mechanical Engineering and Physics.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_the_Registrar_Newsletter_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_the_Registrar_Newsletter-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to the entering class of 2017, Caltech requires students to take a core curriculum of three terms of mathematics, three terms of physics, two terms of chemistry, one term of biology, two terms of lab courses, one terms of scientific communication, three terms of physical education, and 12 terms of humanities and social science.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arms_Laboratory.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Arms_Laboratory.JPG/220px-Arms_Laboratory.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Arms_Laboratory.JPG/330px-Arms_Laboratory.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Arms_Laboratory.JPG/440px-Arms_Laboratory.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arms_Laboratory.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Breezeway of Arms Laboratory</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A typical class is worth 9 academic units and given the extensive core curriculum requirements in addition to individual options' degree requirements, students need to take an average of 40.5 units per term (more than four classes) in order to graduate in four years. 36 units is the minimum full-time load, 48 units is considered a heavy load, and registrations above 54 units require an overload petition.<sup id="cite_ref-fah_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fah-70">[70]</a></sup> Approximately 20 percent of students double-major.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> This is achievable since the humanities and social sciences majors have been designed to be done in conjunction with a science major. Although choosing two options in the same division is discouraged, it is still possible.</p>
<p>First-year students are enrolled in first-term classes based upon results of placement exams in math, physics, chemistry, and writing and take all classes in their first two terms on a Pass/Fail basis.<sup id="cite_ref-fah_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fah-70">[70]</a></sup> There is little competition; collaboration on <a href="/wiki/Homework" title="Homework">homework</a> is encouraged and the Honor System encourages take-home tests and flexible homework schedules.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Caltech offers co-operative programs with other schools, such as the Pasadena <a href="/wiki/Art_Center_College_of_Design" title="Art Center College of Design">Art Center College of Design</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occidental_College" title="Occidental College">Occidental College</a>.</p>
<p>Upon graduation, Caltech alumni have one of the highest median starting salary among graduates of other colleges or universities in 2012–2013, of $67,400, according to <a href="/wiki/PayScale" title="PayScale">PayScale</a>. The mid-career median pay is $120,700.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Caltech was found to offer the second highest return of investment of college education, at $1,991,000 over a 30-year period, according to the same study.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Caltech offers Army and Air Force <a href="/wiki/ROTC" class="mw-redirect" title="ROTC">ROTC</a> in cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cds_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cds-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_program">Graduate program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Graduate program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caltech_regalia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Caltech_regalia.jpg/170px-Caltech_regalia.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Caltech_regalia.jpg/255px-Caltech_regalia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Caltech_regalia.jpg/340px-Caltech_regalia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caltech_regalia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Academic_regalia_in_the_United_States" title="Academic regalia in the United States">Doctoral regalia</a> of the California Institute of Technology</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The graduate instructional programs emphasize doctoral studies and are dominated by science, technology, engineering, and mathematics fields.<sup id="cite_ref-carnegie_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carnegie-51">[51]</a></sup> The Institute offers graduate degree programs for the Master of Science, Engineer's Degree, Doctor of Philosophy, BS/MS and MD/PhD, with the majority of students in the PhD program.<sup id="cite_ref-carnegie_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carnegie-51">[51]</a></sup> The most popular options are Chemistry, Physics, Biology, Electrical Engineering and Chemical Engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_the_Registrar_Newsletter_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_the_Registrar_Newsletter-68">[68]</a></sup> Applicants for graduate studies are required to take the <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Record_Examination" class="mw-redirect" title="Graduate Record Examination">GRE</a>. GRE Subject scores are either required or strongly recommended by several options.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> A joint program between Caltech and the <a href="/wiki/Keck_School_of_Medicine_of_USC" title="Keck School of Medicine of USC">Keck School of Medicine of the University of Southern California</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_David_Geffen_School_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA David Geffen School of Medicine">UCLA David Geffen School of Medicine</a> grants MD/PhD degrees. Students in this program do their preclinical and clinical work at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">USC</a> or <a href="/wiki/UCLA" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA">UCLA</a>, and their PhD work with any member of the Caltech faculty, including the Biology, Chemistry, and Engineering and Applied Sciences Divisions. The MD degree would be from USC or UCLA and the PhD would be awarded from Caltech.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>The research facilities at Caltech are available to graduate students, but there are opportunities for students to work in facilities of other universities, research centers as well as private industries.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The graduate student to faculty ratio is 4:1.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Approximately 99 percent of doctoral students have full financial support. Financial support for graduate students comes in the form of fellowships, research assistantships, teaching assistantships or a combination of fellowship and assistantship support.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Graduate students are bound by the Honor Code, as are the undergraduates, and the Graduate Honor Council oversees any violations of the code.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Caltech was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> in 1934 and remains a research university with "very high" research activity, primarily in <a href="/wiki/STEM_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="STEM fields">STEM fields</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aau_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aau-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-carnegie_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carnegie-51">[51]</a></sup> Caltech manages research expenditures of $270 million annually,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> 66th among all universities in the U.S. and 17th among private institutions without medical schools for 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-nsf_expenditures_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsf_expenditures-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The largest federal agencies contributing to research are <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="United States Department of Health and Human Services">Department of Health and Human Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">Department of Energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Caltech received $144 million in federal funding for the physical sciences, $40.8 million for the life sciences, $33.5 million for engineering, $14.4 million for environmental sciences, $7.16 million for computer sciences, and $1.97 million for mathematical sciences in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Institute was awarded an all-time high funding of $357 million in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-annual_report_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annual_report-86">[86]</a></sup> Active funding from the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> Directorate of Mathematical and Physical Science (MPS) for Caltech stands at $343 million as of 2011, the highest for any educational institution in the nation, and higher than the total funds allocated to any state except California and New York.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SchlingerLabChemE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/SchlingerLabChemE.jpg/220px-SchlingerLabChemE.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/SchlingerLabChemE.jpg/330px-SchlingerLabChemE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/SchlingerLabChemE.jpg/440px-SchlingerLabChemE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SchlingerLabChemE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The new Schlinger Laboratory for Chemistry and Chemical Engineering</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005, Caltech had 739,000 square feet (68,700&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) dedicated to research: 330,000 square feet (30,700&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) to physical sciences, 163,000 square feet (15,100&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) to engineering, and 160,000 square feet (14,900&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) to biological sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to managing JPL, Caltech also operates the <a href="/wiki/Palomar_Observatory" title="Palomar Observatory">Palomar Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County,_California" title="San Diego County, California">San Diego County</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Owens_Valley_Radio_Observatory" title="Owens Valley Radio Observatory">Owens Valley Radio Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bishop,_California" title="Bishop, California">Bishop, California</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caltech_Submillimeter_Observatory" title="Caltech Submillimeter Observatory">Submillimeter Observatory</a> and <a href="/wiki/W._M._Keck_Observatory" title="W. M. Keck Observatory">W. M. Keck Observatory</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Mauna_Kea_Observatory" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauna Kea Observatory">Mauna Kea Observatory</a>, the <a href="/wiki/LIGO" title="LIGO">Laser Interferometer Gravitational-Wave Observatory</a> at <a href="/wiki/Livingston,_Louisiana" title="Livingston, Louisiana">Livingston, Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richland,_Washington" title="Richland, Washington">Richland, Washington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kerckhoff_Marine_Laboratory" title="Kerckhoff Marine Laboratory">Kerckhoff Marine Laboratory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Corona_del_Mar,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Corona del Mar, California">Corona del Mar, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-faculty_handbook_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faculty_handbook-40">[40]</a></sup> The Institute launched the Kavli Nanoscience Institute at Caltech in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-Kavli_Nanoscience_Institute_.28website.29_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kavli_Nanoscience_Institute_.28website.29-89">[89]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Keck_Institute_for_Space_Studies" title="Keck Institute for Space Studies">Keck Institute for Space Studies</a> in 2008, and is also the current home for the <a href="/wiki/Einstein_Papers_Project" title="Einstein Papers Project">Einstein Papers Project</a>. The Spitzer Science Center (SSC), part of the <a href="/wiki/Infrared_Processing_and_Analysis_Center" title="Infrared Processing and Analysis Center">Infrared Processing and Analysis Center</a> located on the Caltech campus, is the data analysis and community support center for <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Spitzer_Space_Telescope" title="Spitzer Space Telescope">Spitzer Space Telescope</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Caltech" class="mw-redirect" title="Caltech">Caltech</a> partnered with <a href="/wiki/UCLA" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA">UCLA</a> to establish a Joint Center for Translational Medicine (UCLA-Caltech JCTM), which conducts experimental research into clinical applications, including the diagnosis and treatment of diseases such as cancer.</p>
<p>Caltech operates several <a href="/wiki/Total_Carbon_Column_Observing_Network" title="Total Carbon Column Observing Network">TCCON</a> stations as part of an international collaborative effort of measuring greenhouse gases globally. One station is on campus.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cahill_Center_for_Astronomy_and_Astrophysics_(_Caltech).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Cahill_Center_for_Astronomy_and_Astrophysics_%28_Caltech%29.jpg/220px-Cahill_Center_for_Astronomy_and_Astrophysics_%28_Caltech%29.jpg" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Cahill_Center_for_Astronomy_and_Astrophysics_%28_Caltech%29.jpg/330px-Cahill_Center_for_Astronomy_and_Astrophysics_%28_Caltech%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Cahill_Center_for_Astronomy_and_Astrophysics_%28_Caltech%29.jpg/440px-Cahill_Center_for_Astronomy_and_Astrophysics_%28_Caltech%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1424" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cahill_Center_for_Astronomy_and_Astrophysics_(_Caltech).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Cahill Center for Astronomy and Astrophysics</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Undergraduates at Caltech are also encouraged to participate in research. About 80% of the class of 2010 did research through the annual <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://surf.caltech.edu/">Summer Undergraduate Research Fellowships (SURF)</a> program at least once during their stay, and many continued during the school year.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Students write and submit SURF proposals for research projects in collaboration with professors, and about 70 percent of applicants are awarded SURFs. The program is open to both Caltech and non-Caltech undergraduate students. It serves as preparation for graduate school and helps to explain why Caltech has the highest percentage of alumni who go on to receive a PhD of all the major universities.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>The licensing and transferring of technology to the commercial sector is managed by the Office of <a href="/wiki/Technology_Transfer" class="mw-redirect" title="Technology Transfer">Technology Transfer</a> (OTT). OTT protects and manages the intellectual property developed by faculty members, students, other researchers, and JPL technologists. Caltech receives more invention disclosures per faculty member than any other university in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> As of 2008, 1891 patents were granted to Caltech researchers since 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="House_system">House system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: House system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">House System at the California Institute of Technology</a></div>
<p>During the early 20th century, a Caltech committee visited several universities and decided to transform the undergraduate housing system from regular <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities">fraternities</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">house system</a>. Four south houses (or <i>hovses</i>) were built: <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology#Blacker_House" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">Blacker House</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology#Dabney_House" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">Dabney House</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology#Fleming_House" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">Fleming House</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology#Ricketts_House" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">Ricketts House</a>. In the 1960s, three north houses were built: <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology#Lloyd_House" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">Lloyd House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Page_House_(Caltech)" class="mw-redirect" title="Page House (Caltech)">Page House</a>, and <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology#Ruddock_House" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">Ruddock House</a>, and during the 1990s, <a href="/wiki/House_System_at_the_California_Institute_of_Technology#Avery_House" title="House System at the California Institute of Technology">Avery House</a>. The four south houses closed for renovation in 2005 and reopened in 2006. All first year students live in the house system and 95% of undergraduates remain affiliated with a house.<sup id="cite_ref-cds_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cds-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-houses_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houses-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beaver_logo_NEW.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1f/Beaver_logo_NEW.jpg/220px-Beaver_logo_NEW.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/1f/Beaver_logo_NEW.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="260" data-file-height="185" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beaver_logo_NEW.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Caltech Beavers' logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Caltech has athletic teams in baseball, men's and women's basketball, cross country, fencing, men's soccer, swimming and diving, men's and women's tennis, track and field, women's volleyball, and men's and women's water polo.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Caltech's mascot is the Beaver, a homage to nature's engineer.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Its teams (with the exception of the fencing team) play in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Intercollegiate_Athletic_Conference" title="Southern California Intercollegiate Athletic Conference">Southern California Intercollegiate Athletic Conference</a>, which Caltech co-founded in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The fencing team<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> competes in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a>, facing teams from <a href="/wiki/UCLA" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA">UCLA</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">USC</a>, <a href="/wiki/UCSD" class="mw-redirect" title="UCSD">UCSD</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stanford" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanford">Stanford</a>, among others.</p>
<p>On January 6, 2007, the Beavers' men's basketball team snapped a 207-game losing streak to Division III schools, beating <a href="/wiki/Bard_College" title="Bard College">Bard College</a> 81–52. It was their first Division III victory since 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Until their win over Occidental on February 22, 2011<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> the team had not won a game in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Intercollegiate_Athletic_Conference" title="Southern California Intercollegiate Athletic Conference">conference</a> play since 1985. Ryan Elmquist's free throw with 3.3 seconds in regulation gave the Beavers the victory.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Quantum_Hoops" title="Quantum Hoops">Quantum Hoops</a></i> concerns the events of the Beavers' 2005–06 season.</p>
<p>On January 13, 2007, the Caltech women's basketball team snapped a 50-game losing streak, defeating the <a href="/wiki/Claremont_Colleges" title="Claremont Colleges">Pomona–Pitzer</a> Sagehens 55–53. The women's program, which entered the <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Intercollegiate_Athletic_Conference" title="Southern California Intercollegiate Athletic Conference">SCIAC</a> in 2002, garnered their first conference win. On the bench as honorary coach for the evening was <a href="/wiki/Robert_Grubbs" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Grubbs">Dr. Robert Grubbs</a>, 2005 Nobel laureate in Chemistry.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The team went on to beat Whittier College on February 10, for its second SCIAC win, and placed its first member on the All Conference team.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The 2006–2007 season is the most successful season in the history of the program.</p>
<p>In 2007, 2008, and 2009, the women's table tennis team (a club team) competed in nationals. The women's <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">Ultimate</a> club team, known as "Snatch", has also been very successful in recent years, ranking 44 of over 200 college teams in the Ultimate Player's Association.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 2, 2013, the Caltech baseball team ended a 228-game losing streak, the team's first win in nearly 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>The track and field team plays at the South Athletic Field in <a href="/wiki/Tournament_Park" title="Tournament Park">Tournament Park</a>, the site of the first <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl Game</a>.</p>
<p>The school also sponsored a football team prior to 1976, which played part of its home schedule at the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(stadium)" title="Rose Bowl (stadium)">Rose Bowl</a>, or, as Caltech students put it, "to the largest number of empty seats in the nation".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_and_visual_arts">Performing and visual arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Performing and visual arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Caltech/<a href="/wiki/Occidental_College" title="Occidental College">Occidental College</a> Orchestra is a full seventy-piece orchestra composed of students, faculty, and staff at Caltech and nearby Occidental College. The orchestra gives three pairs of concerts annually, at both Caltech and Occidental College. There are also two Caltech Jazz Bands and a Concert Band. For vocal music, Caltech has a mixed voice <a href="/wiki/Glee_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Glee Club">Glee Club</a> and a smaller <a href="/wiki/Chamber_Singer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber Singer">Chamber Singer</a> group.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The theater program at Caltech is known as TACIT, or Theater Arts at the California Institute of Technology. There are two to three plays organized by TACIT per year, and they were involved in the production of the <a href="/wiki/PHD_Comics#Piled_Higher_and_Deeper:_the_Movie" class="mw-redirect" title="PHD Comics">PHD Movie</a>, released in 2011.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life_traditions">Student life traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Student life traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_events">Annual events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Annual events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Every <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a>, Dabney House conducts the infamous "Millikan pumpkin-drop experiment" from the top of Millikan Library, the highest point on campus. According to tradition, a claim was once made that the shattering of a pumpkin frozen in <a href="/wiki/Liquid_nitrogen" title="Liquid nitrogen">liquid nitrogen</a> and dropped from a sufficient height would produce a <a href="/wiki/Triboluminescence" title="Triboluminescence">triboluminescent</a> spark. This yearly event involves a crowd of observers, who try to spot the elusive spark. The title of the event is an oblique reference to the famous <a href="/wiki/Oil-drop_experiment" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil-drop experiment">Millikan oil-drop experiment</a> which measured <i>e</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Elementary_charge" title="Elementary charge">elemental unit of electrical charge</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beckman_auditorium,_Caltech.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Beckman_auditorium%2C_Caltech.jpg/220px-Beckman_auditorium%2C_Caltech.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Beckman_auditorium%2C_Caltech.jpg/330px-Beckman_auditorium%2C_Caltech.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Beckman_auditorium%2C_Caltech.jpg/440px-Beckman_auditorium%2C_Caltech.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beckman_auditorium,_Caltech.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Beckman Auditorium</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On Ditch Day, the seniors ditch school, leaving behind elaborately designed tasks and traps at the doors of their rooms to prevent underclassmen from entering. Over the years this has evolved to the point where many seniors spend months designing mechanical, electrical, and software obstacles to confound the underclassmen. Each group of seniors designs a "stack" to be solved by a handful of underclassmen. The faculty have been drawn into the event as well, and cancel all classes on Ditch Day so the underclassmen can participate in what has become a highlight of the academic year.</p>
<p>Another long-standing tradition is the playing of Wagner's "<a href="/wiki/Ride_of_the_Valkyries" title="Ride of the Valkyries">Ride of the Valkyries</a>" at 7:00 each morning during finals week with the largest, loudest speakers available. The playing of that piece is not allowed at any other time (except if one happens to be listening to the entire 14 hours and 5 minutes of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ring_Cycle" class="mw-redirect" title="The Ring Cycle">The Ring Cycle</a></i>), and any offender is dragged into the showers to be drenched in cold water fully dressed. The playing of the <i>Ride</i> is such a strong tradition that the music was used during <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">Apollo 17</a> to awaken Astronaut <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Schmitt" title="Harrison Schmitt">Harrison Schmitt</a>, a Caltech alumnus. Unfortunately, the tradition arose at different times in different Houses, so Schmitt did not react as expected. Instead, he just became confused.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pranks">Pranks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Pranks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fleming_cannon_firing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fleming_cannon_firing.jpg/220px-Fleming_cannon_firing.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fleming_cannon_firing.jpg/330px-Fleming_cannon_firing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fleming_cannon_firing.jpg/440px-Fleming_cannon_firing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fleming_cannon_firing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Fleming cannon</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Caltech students have been known for the many <a href="/wiki/Student_prank" title="Student prank">pranks</a> (also known as "RFs").<sup id="cite_ref-Caltech1_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caltech1-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>The two most famous in recent history are the changing of the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Sign" title="Hollywood Sign">Hollywood Sign</a> to read "Caltech", by judiciously covering up certain parts of the letters, and the changing of the scoreboard to read Caltech 38, MIT 9 during the <a href="/wiki/1984_Rose_Bowl" title="1984 Rose Bowl">1984 Rose Bowl Game</a>. But the most famous of all occurred during the <a href="/wiki/1961_Rose_Bowl" title="1961 Rose Bowl">1961 Rose Bowl Game</a>, where Caltech students altered the flip-cards that were raised by the stadium attendees to display "Caltech", and several other "unintended" messages. This event is now referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rose_Bowl_Hoax" title="Great Rose Bowl Hoax">Great Rose Bowl Hoax</a>.</p>
<p>In recent years, pranking has been officially encouraged by Tom Mannion, Caltech's Assistant VP for Student Affairs and Campus Life. "The grand old days of pranking have gone away at Caltech, and that's what we are trying to bring back," reported the <i>Boston Globe</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2011, Caltech students went to New York and pulled a prank on Manhattan's <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a>. The prank involved making <a href="/wiki/Alamo_(sculpture)" title="Alamo (sculpture)">The Cube</a> sculpture look like the <a href="/wiki/Aperture_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="Aperture Science">Aperture Science</a> Weighted Companion Cube from the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Portal_(video_game)" title="Portal (video game)">Portal</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Caltech pranks have been documented in three Legends of Caltech books, the most recent of which was edited by alumni Autumn Looijen '99 and Mason A. Porter '98 and published in May 2007.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_MIT">Rivalry with MIT</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rivalry with MIT">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Caltech%E2%80%93MIT_rivalry" title="Caltech–MIT rivalry">Caltech–MIT rivalry</a></div>
<p>In 2005, a group of Caltech students pulled a string of pranks during MIT's Campus Preview Weekend for admitted students. These include covering up the word Massachusetts in the "Massachusetts Institute of Technology" engraving on the main building façade with a banner so that it read "That Other Institute of Technology". A group of <a href="/wiki/Hacks_at_the_Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Hacks at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT hackers</a> responded by altering the banner so that the inscription read "The Only Institute of Technology." Caltech students also passed out T-shirts to MIT's incoming freshman class that had MIT written on the front and "... because not everyone can go to Caltech" along with an image of a palm tree on the back.</p>
<p>MIT retaliated in April 2006, when students posing as the Howe &amp; Ser (Howitzer) Moving Company stole the 130-year-old, 1.7-ton Fleming House cannon and moved it over 3000 miles to their campus in Cambridge, Massachusetts for their 2006 Campus Preview Weekend, repeating a similar prank performed by nearby <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Mudd_College" title="Harvey Mudd College">Harvey Mudd College</a> in 1986. Thirty members of Fleming House traveled to MIT and reclaimed their cannon on April 10, 2006.</p>
<p>On April 13, 2007 (Friday the 13th), a group of students from <i>The California Tech</i>, Caltech's campus newspaper, arrived and distributed fake copies of <i>The Tech</i>, MIT's campus newspaper, while prospective students were visiting for their Campus Preview Weekend. Articles included "MIT Invents the Interweb", "Architects Deem Campus 'Unfortunate'", and "Infinite Corridor Not Actually Infinite".</p>
<p>In December 2009, some Caltech students declared that MIT had been sold and had become the Caltech East campus. A "sold" banner was hung on front of the MIT dome building and a "Welcome to Caltech East: School of the Humanities" banner over the Massachusetts Avenue Entrance. Newspapers and T-shirts were distributed, and door labels and fliers in the infinite corridor were put up in accordance with the "curriculum change."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2010, MIT students attempted to put a <a href="/wiki/TARDIS" title="TARDIS">TARDIS</a>, the time machine from the BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i>, onto a roof. Caught in midact, the prank was aborted. In January 2011, Caltech students in conjunction with MIT students helped put the TARDIS on top of Baxter.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Caltech students then moved the TARDIS to <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" class="mw-redirect" title="UC Berkeley">UC Berkeley</a><sup id="cite_ref-Alessondra_Springmann.2C_PCWorld_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alessondra_Springmann.2C_PCWorld-114">[114]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Stanford" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanford">Stanford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2014, during MIT's Campus Preview Weekend, a group of Caltech students handed out mugs emblazoned with the MIT logo on the front and the words "The Institute of Technology" on the back. When heated, the mugs turn orange, display a palm tree, and read "Caltech The Hotter Institute of Technology." Identical mugs continue to be sold at the Caltech campus store.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Honor_code">Honor code</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Honor code">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Life in the Caltech community is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Honor_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Honor code">honor code</a>, which simply states: "No member of the Caltech community shall take unfair advantage of any other member of the Caltech community." This is enforced by a Board of Control, which consists of undergraduate students,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and by a similar body at the graduate level, called the Graduate Honor Council.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>The honor code aims at promoting an atmosphere of respect and trust that allows Caltech students to enjoy privileges that make for a more relaxed atmosphere. For example, the honor code allows professors to make the majority of exams as take-home, allowing students to take them on their own schedule and in their preferred environment.</p>
<p>Through the late 1990s, the only exception to the honor code, implemented earlier in the decade in response to changes in federal regulations, concerned the sexual harassment policy. Today, there are myriad exceptions to the honor code in the form of new institute policies such as the fire policy, and alcohol policy. Though both policies are presented in the Honor System Handbook given to new members of the Caltech community, some undergraduates regard them as a slight against the honor code and the implicit trust and respect it represents within the community.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: People">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_California_Institute_of_Technology_people" title="List of California Institute of Technology people">List of California Institute of Technology people</a></div>
<p>As of 2015, Caltech has 34 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureates</a> to its name. This figure includes 20 alumni, 14 non-alumni professors, and 4 professors who are also alumni (<a href="/wiki/Carl_D._Anderson" class="mw-redirect" title="Carl D. Anderson">Carl D. Anderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linus_Pauling" title="Linus Pauling">Linus Pauling</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_A._Fowler" class="mw-redirect" title="William A. Fowler">William A. Fowler</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edward_B._Lewis" title="Edward B. Lewis">Edward B. Lewis</a>). The number of awards is 35, because Pauling received prizes in both <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Chemistry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Peace" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in Peace">Peace</a>. Seven faculty and alumni have received a <a href="/wiki/Crafoord_Prize" title="Crafoord Prize">Crafoord Prize</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a>, while 58 have been awarded the U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>, and 13 have received the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="National Medal of Technology">National Medal of Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-at_a_glance_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at_a_glance-4">[4]</a></sup> One alumnus, <a href="/wiki/Stanislav_Smirnov" title="Stanislav Smirnov">Stanislav Smirnov</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a> in 2010. Other distinguished researchers have been affiliated with Caltech as postdoctoral scholars (for example, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_McClintock" title="Barbara McClintock">Barbara McClintock</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_D._Watson" class="mw-redirect" title="James D. Watson">James D. Watson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Glashow" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheldon Glashow">Sheldon Glashow</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Gurdon" title="John Gurdon">John Gurdon</a>) or visiting professors (for example, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Witten" title="Edward Witten">Edward Witten</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Students">Students</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Students">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Caltech enrolled 979 undergraduate students and 1,261 graduate students for the 2016–2017 school year. Women made up 41% of the undergraduate and 29% of the graduate student body.<sup id="cite_ref-enrollment_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enrollment-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The four-year graduation rate is 79% and the six-year rate is 92%,<sup id="cite_ref-cds_54-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cds-54">[54]</a></sup> which is low compared to most leading U.S. universities,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> but substantially higher than it was in the 1960s and 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Students majoring in <a href="/wiki/STEM_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="STEM fields">STEM fields</a> traditionally have graduation rates below 70%.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_and_staff">Faculty and staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Faculty and staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Broad_center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Broad_center.jpg/220px-Broad_center.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Broad_center.jpg/330px-Broad_center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Broad_center.jpg/440px-Broad_center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Broad_center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Broad Center for Biological Sciences</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Richard_Feynman" title="Richard Feynman">Richard Feynman</a> was among the most well-known physicists associated with Caltech, having published the <i><a href="/wiki/Feynman_Lectures_on_Physics" class="mw-redirect" title="Feynman Lectures on Physics">Feynman Lectures on Physics</a></i>, an undergraduate physics text, and a few other popular science texts such as <i><a href="/wiki/Six_Easy_Pieces#Six_Easy_Pieces_.281994.29" class="mw-redirect" title="Six Easy Pieces">Six Easy Pieces</a></i> for the general audience. The promotion of physics made him a public figure of science, although his Nobel-winning work in <a href="/wiki/Quantum_electrodynamics" title="Quantum electrodynamics">quantum electrodynamics</a> was already very established in the scientific community. <a href="/wiki/Murray_Gell-Mann" title="Murray Gell-Mann">Murray Gell-Mann</a>, a Nobel-winning physicist, introduced a classification of <a href="/wiki/Hadrons" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadrons">hadrons</a> and went on to postulate the existence of <a href="/wiki/Quark" title="Quark">quarks</a>, which is currently accepted as part of the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Model" title="Standard Model">Standard Model</a>. Long-time Caltech President <a href="/wiki/Robert_Andrews_Millikan" title="Robert Andrews Millikan">Robert Andrews Millikan</a> was the first to calculate the charge of the <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">electron</a> with his well-known <a href="/wiki/Oil-drop_experiment" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil-drop experiment">oil-drop experiment</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Richard_Chace_Tolman" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Chace Tolman">Richard Chace Tolman</a> is remembered for his contributions to <a href="/wiki/Cosmology" title="Cosmology">cosmology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">statistical mechanics</a>. 2004 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> winner <a href="/wiki/H._David_Politzer" class="mw-redirect" title="H. David Politzer">H. David Politzer</a> is a current professor at Caltech, as is astrophysicist and author <a href="/wiki/Kip_Thorne" title="Kip Thorne">Kip Thorne</a> and eminent mathematician <a href="/wiki/Barry_Simon" title="Barry Simon">Barry Simon</a>. <a href="/wiki/Linus_Pauling" title="Linus Pauling">Linus Pauling</a> pioneered <a href="/wiki/Quantum_chemistry" title="Quantum chemistry">quantum chemistry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular biology</a>, and went on to discover the nature of the chemical bond in 1939. Seismologist <a href="/wiki/Charles_Richter" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Richter">Charles Richter</a>, also an alumnus, developed the magnitude scale that bears his name, the <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">Richter magnitude scale</a> for measuring the power of earthquakes. One of the founders of the geochemistry department, <a href="/wiki/Clair_Patterson" class="mw-redirect" title="Clair Patterson">Clair Patterson</a> was the first to accurately determine the age of the Earth via lead:uranium ratio in meteorites. In engineering, <a href="/wiki/Theodore_von_K%C3%A1rm%C3%A1n" title="Theodore von Kármán">Theodore von Kármán</a> made many key advances in aerodynamics, notably his work on <a href="/wiki/Supersonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Supersonic">supersonic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hypersonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypersonic">hypersonic</a> airflow characterization. A repeating pattern of swirling <a href="/wiki/Vortices" class="mw-redirect" title="Vortices">vortices</a> is named after him, the <a href="/wiki/Von_K%C3%A1rm%C3%A1n_vortex_street" class="mw-redirect" title="Von Kármán vortex street">von Kármán vortex street</a>. Participants in von Kármán's GALCIT project included <a href="/wiki/Frank_Malina" title="Frank Malina">Frank Malina</a>, who helped develop the <a href="/wiki/WAC_Corporal" title="WAC Corporal">WAC Corporal</a> which was the first U.S. rocket to reach the edge of space, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Parsons_(rocket_engineer)" title="Jack Parsons (rocket engineer)">Jack Parsons</a>, a pioneer in the development of liquid and solid rocket fuels who designed the first castable composite-based rocket motor, and <a href="/wiki/Qian_Xuesen" title="Qian Xuesen">Qian Xuesen</a>, who was dubbed the "Father of Chinese Rocketry". More recently, <a href="/wiki/Michael_E._Brown" title="Michael E. Brown">Michael Brown</a>, a professor of planetary astronomy, discovered many <a href="/wiki/Trans-Neptunian_object" title="Trans-Neptunian object">trans-Neptunian objects</a>, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planet</a> <a href="/wiki/Eris_(dwarf_planet)" title="Eris (dwarf planet)">Eris</a>, which prompted the <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">International Astronomical Union</a> to redefine the term "<a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a>".</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Baltimore" title="David Baltimore">David Baltimore</a>, the Robert A. Millikan Professor of Biology, and <a href="/wiki/Alice_S._Huang" title="Alice S. Huang">Alice Huang</a>, Senior Faculty Associate in Biology, have served as the President of <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">AAAS</a> from 2007–2008 and 2010–2011 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>33% of the faculty are members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="National Academy of Science">National Academy of Science</a> or <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">Engineering</a> and/or fellows of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>. This is the highest percentage of any faculty in the country with the exception of the graduate institution <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_University" title="Rockefeller University">Rockefeller University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average salary for assistant professors at Caltech is $111,300, associate professors $121,300, and full professors $172,800.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Caltech faculty are active in applied physics, astronomy and astrophysics, biology, biochemistry, biological engineering, chemical engineering, computer science, geology, mechanical engineering and physics.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=California_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are 22,930 total living alumni in the U.S. and around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> 20 alumni and 14 non-alumni faculty have won the Nobel Prize. The <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a>, the "Nobel Prize of Computer Science", has been awarded to six alumni, and one has won the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-science_now_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-science_now-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alumni have participated in scientific research. Some have concentrated their studies on the very small universe of atoms and molecules. <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureate</a> <a href="/wiki/Carl_D._Anderson" class="mw-redirect" title="Carl D. Anderson">Carl D. Anderson</a> (BS 1927, PhD 1930) proved the existence of <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">positrons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muon" title="Muon">muons</a>, Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Edwin_McMillan" title="Edwin McMillan">Edwin McMillan</a> (BS 1928, MS 1929) synthesized the first <a href="/wiki/Transuranium_element" title="Transuranium element">transuranium element</a>, Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Leo_James_Rainwater" class="mw-redirect" title="Leo James Rainwater">Leo James Rainwater</a> (BS 1939) investigated the non-spherical shapes of atomic nuclei, and Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Douglas_D._Osheroff" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas D. Osheroff">Douglas D. Osheroff</a> (BS 1967) studied the <a href="/wiki/Superfluid" class="mw-redirect" title="Superfluid">superfluid</a> nature of <a href="/wiki/Helium-3" title="Helium-3">helium-3</a>. <a href="/wiki/Donald_Knuth" title="Donald Knuth">Donald Knuth</a> (PhD 1963), the "father" of the <a href="/wiki/Analysis_of_algorithms" title="Analysis of algorithms">analysis of algorithms</a>, wrote <i><a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Computer_Programming" title="The Art of Computer Programming">The Art of Computer Programming</a></i> and created the <a href="/wiki/TeX" title="TeX">TeX</a> computer typesetting system, which is commonly used in the scientific community. <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Karmarkar" title="Narendra Karmarkar">Narendra Karmarkar</a> (MS 1979) is known for the interior point method, a polynomial algorithm for linear programming known as <a href="/wiki/Karmarkar%27s_algorithm" title="Karmarkar's algorithm">Karmarkar's algorithm</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caltech_from_the_air.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Caltech_from_the_air.jpg/220px-Caltech_from_the_air.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Caltech_from_the_air.jpg/330px-Caltech_from_the_air.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Caltech_from_the_air.jpg/440px-Caltech_from_the_air.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caltech_from_the_air.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of Caltech in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other alumni have turned their gaze to the universe. <a href="/wiki/C._Gordon_Fullerton" title="C. Gordon Fullerton">C. Gordon Fullerton</a> (BS 1957, MS 1958) piloted the third <a href="/wiki/Space_shuttle" class="mw-redirect" title="Space shuttle">space shuttle</a> mission and orbited the earth in <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">Skylab</a>. Astronaut (and later, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senator" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Senator">United States Senator</a>) <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Schmitt" title="Harrison Schmitt">Harrison Schmitt</a> (BS 1957) was the only geologist to have ever walked on the surface of the moon.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Astronomer <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Merle_Shoemaker" title="Eugene Merle Shoemaker">Eugene Merle Shoemaker</a> (BS 1947, MS 1948) co-discovered <a href="/wiki/Comet_Shoemaker-Levy_9" class="mw-redirect" title="Comet Shoemaker-Levy 9">Comet Shoemaker-Levy 9</a> (a comet which crashed into the planet <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>) and was the first person buried on the moon (by having his ashes crashed into the moon).<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Undergraduate alumni founded, or co-founded, companies such as <a href="/wiki/LCD" class="mw-redirect" title="LCD">LCD</a> manufacturer Varitronix,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hotmail" class="mw-redirect" title="Hotmail">Hotmail</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Compaq" title="Compaq">Compaq</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MathWorks" title="MathWorks">MathWorks</a> (which created <a href="/wiki/Matlab" class="mw-redirect" title="Matlab">Matlab</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> while graduate students founded, or co-founded, companies such as <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TRW_Inc." title="TRW Inc.">TRW</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> and the non-profit educational organization, the <a href="/wiki/Exploratorium" title="Exploratorium">Exploratorium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arnold_Orville_Beckman" title="Arnold Orville Beckman">Arnold Beckman</a> (PhD 1928) invented the <a href="/wiki/PH_meter" title="PH meter">pH meter</a> and commercialized it with the founding of <a href="/wiki/Beckman_Instruments" class="mw-redirect" title="Beckman Instruments">Beckman Instruments</a>. His success with that company enabled him to provide seed funding for <a href="/wiki/William_Shockley" title="William Shockley">William Shockley</a> (BS 1932), who had co-invented <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor" title="Semiconductor">semiconductor</a> <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">transistors</a> and wanted to commercialize them. Shockley became the founding Director of the <a href="/wiki/Shockley_Semiconductor_Laboratory" title="Shockley Semiconductor Laboratory">Shockley Semiconductor Laboratory</a> division of Beckman Instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-Shockley_byNobelPrizeFoundation1956_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shockley_byNobelPrizeFoundation1956-138">[138]</a></sup> Shockley had previously worked at <a href="/wiki/Bell_Labs" title="Bell Labs">Bell Labs</a>, whose first president was another alumnus, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Jewett" class="mw-redirect" title="Frank Jewett">Frank Jewett</a> (BS 1898). Because his aging mother lived in <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">Palo Alto, California</a>, Shockley established his laboratory near her in <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">Mountain View, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Shockley_byNobelPrizeFoundation1956_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shockley_byNobelPrizeFoundation1956-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Shockley was a co-recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_physics" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in physics">Nobel Prize in physics</a> in 1956, but his aggressive management style and odd personality<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> at the Shockley Lab became unbearable.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> In late 1957, eight of his researchers resigned and with support from <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Fairchild" title="Sherman Fairchild">Sherman Fairchild</a> formed <a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Semiconductor" title="Fairchild Semiconductor">Fairchild Semiconductor</a>. Among the "<a href="/wiki/Traitorous_eight" title="Traitorous eight">traitorous eight</a>" was <a href="/wiki/Gordon_E._Moore" class="mw-redirect" title="Gordon E. Moore">Gordon E. Moore</a> (PhD 1954), who later left Fairchild to co-found <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>. Other offspring companies of Fairchild Semiconductor include <a href="/wiki/National_Semiconductor" title="National Semiconductor">National Semiconductor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Micro_Devices" title="Advanced Micro Devices">Advanced Micro Devices</a>, which in turn spawned more technology companies in the area. Shockley's decision to use <a href="/wiki/Silicon" title="Silicon">silicon</a> – instead of <a href="/wiki/Germanium" title="Germanium">germanium</a> – as the <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor" title="Semiconductor">semiconductor</a> material, coupled with the abundance of silicon semiconductor related companies in the area, gave rise to the term "<a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> to describe that geographic region surrounding Palo Alto.</p>
<p>Caltech alumni also held public offices, with <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_A.G._Abushagur" title="Mustafa A.G. Abushagur">Mustafa A.G. Abushagur</a> (PhD 1984) the Deputy Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_C._Fletcher" title="James C. Fletcher">James Fletcher</a> (PhD 1948) the 4th and 7th <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_NASA" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrator of NASA">Administrator of NASA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steven_E._Koonin" title="Steven E. Koonin">Steven Koonin</a> (PhD 1972) the <a href="/wiki/Under_Secretary_of_Energy_for_Science" title="Under Secretary of Energy for Science">Undersecretary of Energy for Science</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Regina_E._Dugan" title="Regina E. Dugan">Regina Dugan</a> (PhD 1993) the 19th director of <a href="/wiki/DARPA" title="DARPA">DARPA</a>. The 20th director for DARPA, <a href="/wiki/Arati_Prabhakar" title="Arati Prabhakar">Arati Prabhakar</a>, is also a Caltech alumna (PhD 1984). <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Virmani" title="Arvind Virmani">Arvind Virmani</a> is a former <a href="/wiki/Chief_Economic_Adviser_to_the_Government_of_India" title="Chief Economic Adviser to the Government of India">Chief Economic Adviser to the Government of India</a>. In 2013, President Obama announced the nomination of <a href="/wiki/France_Cordova" class="mw-redirect" title="France Cordova">France Cordova</a> (PhD 1979) as the director of the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> and Ellen Williams (PhD 1982) as the director for <a href="/wiki/ARPA-E" title="ARPA-E">ARPA-E</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>

<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 165px">

<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">
<div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr_Mustafa_Abushagur.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Dr_Mustafa_Abushagur.JPG/90px-Dr_Mustafa_Abushagur.JPG" width="90" height="130" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Dr_Mustafa_Abushagur.JPG/135px-Dr_Mustafa_Abushagur.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Dr_Mustafa_Abushagur.JPG/180px-Dr_Mustafa_Abushagur.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1960" data-file-height="2828" /></a></div>
